**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

Summarizing: 

Keep all areas and topics in their original orders determined in Step 4. For each topic, write an summary paragraph as if you are doing an academic study of the headlines. Choosing your length appropriately by importance and complexity of that topic. You should learn from all the headlines, and especially the ones with high importance scores under the topic, discover their connections, and put everything into a coherent narrative, and provide citations (the IDs of news articles) for your claims. You need to cover the main ideas behind all the articles, but you don't need to cite every single of them. You only cite the meaningful, high-quality sources. You should never use overly broad, generic phrasing, which is a mistake you often make. Keep tone urgent, stick to the facts, use concrete examples, be razor sharp, be non-partisan. Do not offer policy recommendations. No editorializing or speculation — stick strictly to facts in the JSON. Sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. In that case, keep to what the headlines explicitly say, and explain that information is insufficient, and keep the summary brief. Do not make your own guesses to fill up the space!

**Please be super aware of the possibility of hallucinations!** That is absolutely not allowed. This is a common problem for LLMs like you. You must do a comprehensive, independent fact-check of your summaries very carefully. Every name, job title, date, event, quote, and other facts should be exactly as what you learned from the news headlines. Be fully aware that your internal knowledge base is outdated.

After your summary, paste the entire JSON lines of the news articles you cited in the summary paragraph, directly under your summaries. This is the same for all other topics under an area and also all other areas. Compile all your results in a simple text file (step5.txt). After you finish with the file, briefly explain the revisions you made.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

**DAILY BRIEFING FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP**
**June 2025**

**OVERVIEW**

The United States has executed Operation "Midnight Hammer," a direct military strike against Iran's nuclear infrastructure, precipitating an immediate and multifaceted international crisis. The administration has narrowly defined the action as a war targeting Iran’s nuclear program, not the nation itself, but this distinction is not universally accepted at home or abroad. The strikes have prompted the Department of Homeland Security to issue a national terrorism bulletin for a "heightened threat environment," triggered a significant global oil price surge, and ignited a contentious constitutional debate in Congress over the legality of the President's actions. Compounding the crisis are reports of internal discord within the White House national security team and significant, public fractures among the President’s political allies, creating a volatile and unpredictable strategic environment.

**Area 1: U.S. Military Action in Iran**

**Topic 1.1: Operation "Midnight Hammer": Execution and Official Justification**

The United States has conducted a "devastating stealth strike" against Iran, codenamed "Operation Midnight Hammer" [1, 2]. The operation was substantial in scale, involving seven B-2 stealth bombers that deployed 14 specialized bunker-buster munitions, and was reportedly overseen by U.S. General Michael Kurilla [3, 4]. The administration is framing the military action with specific, carefully chosen language to manage its strategic scope. Vice President JD Vance articulated the official position by stating, "U.S. isn’t at war with Iran, ‘we’re at war with Iran’s nuclear program’" [5]. This justification is being highlighted by media outlets as a new rationale for military engagement, particularly as it appears to contrast with President Trump’s previous campaign promises to keep the U.S. out of new wars in the Middle East [6].

**DAILY BRIEFING FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP**
**June 2025**

**OVERVIEW**

The United States has executed Operation "Midnight Hammer," a direct military strike against Iran's nuclear infrastructure, precipitating an immediate and multifaceted international crisis. The administration has narrowly defined the action as a war targeting Iran’s nuclear program, not the nation itself, but this distinction is not universally accepted at home or abroad. The strikes have prompted the Department of Homeland Security to issue a national terrorism bulletin for a "heightened threat environment," triggered a significant global oil price surge, and ignited a contentious constitutional debate in Congress over the legality of the President's actions. Compounding the crisis are reports of internal discord within the White House national security team and significant, public fractures among the President’s political allies, creating a volatile and unpredictable strategic environment.

---

**Area 1: U.S. Military Action in Iran**

**Topic 1.1: Operation "Midnight Hammer": Execution and Official Justification**

The United States has conducted a "devastating stealth strike" against Iran, codenamed "Operation Midnight Hammer" [1, 2]. The operation was substantial in scale, involving seven B-2 stealth bombers that deployed 14 specialized bunker-buster munitions, and was reportedly overseen by U.S. General Michael Kurilla [3, 4]. The administration is framing the military action with specific, carefully chosen language to manage its strategic scope. Vice President JD Vance articulated the official position by stating, "U.S. isn’t at war with Iran, ‘we’re at war with Iran’s nuclear program’" [5]. This justification is being highlighted by media outlets as a new rationale for military engagement, particularly as it appears to contrast with President Trump’s previous campaign promises to keep the U.S. out of new wars in the Middle East [6].

*References:*
[1] How Trump unleashed devastating ‘Midnight Hammer ‘ stealth strike on Iran using deception as key weapon, https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/trump-bombs-iran-midnight-hammer-b2774686.html

[2] "Operation Midnight Hammer": What we know about the Iran strikes, https://www.newsweek.com/operation-midnight-hammer-what-we-know-about-iran-strikes-2088954

[3] U.S. used 14 bunker-busters, 7 B-2 bombers in "Midnight Hammer" strikes on Iran, https://www.axios.com/2025/06/22/iran-nuclear-midnight-hammer-bunker-buster

[5] U.S. isn’t at war with Iran, ‘we’re at war with Iran’s nuclear program,’ Vance says, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/06/22/vance-us-is-at-war-with-irans-nuclear-program.html

[6] Trump Promised To Keep The U.S. Out Of Middle East Wars. Now Vance Has A New Justification., https://www.huffpost.com/entry/jd-vance-dumb-presidents-trump-iran-middle-east_n_68584913e4b0208df3862856?utm_medium=Social&utm_source=reddit&utm_campaign=us_main

**Topic 1.2: Intelligence and Military Assessments of the Strikes**

Initial battlefield damage assessments from the Pentagon are preliminary and inconclusive. While satellite imagery indicates Iran's Fordo nuclear site looks "severely damaged," it is reportedly not completely destroyed [1]. Pentagon officials have publicly stated that it is "too soon to know if Iran strikes were successful," and early U.S. intelligence reports are raising significant questions as to whether the "bulk of enriched Iranian nuclear material" was actually destroyed in the attack [2, 3]. The intelligence foundation for the operation is also facing sharp external scrutiny. One critical report, citing anonymous sources, claims, "‘There Is No Intel’: Trump’s Attacks on Iran Were Based on Vibes" [4]. A separate piece of commentary offers a different view, suggesting that while President Trump himself may have changed his approach to foreign entanglements, "The Intelligence Didn’t," implying the basis for action was pre-existing [5].

*References:*
[1] Iran’s Fordo Site Said to Look Severely Damaged, Not Destroyed, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/06/22/world/middleeast/iran-fordo-nuclear-damaged-not-destroyed.html

[2] ‘Severe damage’: Pentagon officials say it’s too soon to know if Iran strikes were successful, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/06/22/severe-damage-pentagon-iran-strikes-00416557

[3] Early assessments raise questions over whether US destroyed bulk of enriched Iranian nuclear material, https://www.cnn.com/2025/06/22/politics/iran-strike-analysis-raises-questions

[4] ‘There Is No Intel’: Trump’s Attacks on Iran Were Based on Vibes, Sources Say, https://www.rollingstone.com/politics/politics-features/trump-iran-attack-no-intel-nuclear-1235369641/

[5] Trump Changed. The Intelligence Didn’t., https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2025/06/trump-changed-the-intelligence-didnt/683289/

**Topic 1.3: White House and Pentagon Crisis Management**

The administration's public messaging on the ultimate goal of the strikes appears conflicted, suggesting a lack of a unified strategy. President Trump has openly and publicly posted messages questioning "why there would not be 'regime change' in Iran" [1]. This posture contrasts sharply with that of Secretary of State Marco Rubio, who stated the "U.S. is ready to meet with Iran after strikes" while also delivering a stark warning that any Iranian attempt to close the Strait of Hormuz would be "suicidal" [2]. Reports also indicate significant internal friction within the national security team. Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard was reportedly excluded from Situation Room photos during the operation and is said to be "on the outs with president" ever since she posted a video online warning against "political elites and warmongers" [3].

*References:*
[1] Trump asks why there would not be 'regime change' in Iran, https://www.reuters.com/world/trump-asks-why-there-would-not-be-regime-change-iran-2025-06-22/

[2] Rubio says U.S. is ready to meet with Iran after strikes, warns closing Strait of Hormuz would be "suicidal", https://www.cbsnews.com/news/marco-rubio-iran-strikes-nuclear-hormuz-face-the-nation/

**Area 2: International Ramifications of the U.S. Strikes**

**Topic 2.1: Global Diplomatic Reactions and Iranian Response**

The U.S. strikes have triggered sharp international condemnation and threats of dangerous escalation. In a particularly severe development, Russia has publicly claimed that other unnamed nations are now "ready to supply Iran with nukes" in the direct aftermath of the U.S. action [1]. In a bid to control the economic fallout, the U.S. has publicly urged China to leverage its influence to "dissuade Iran from closing Strait of Hormuz" [2]. This diplomatic outreach comes as Iran's parliament has reportedly backed measures to do just that, with Iranian Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi warning of "everlasting consequences" for the strikes [3, 4]. Meanwhile, reports from inside Iran describe a population that feels "'paralysed and constantly caught by surprise'" by the attack [5]. In another significant diplomatic reversal, Pakistan issued a statement condemning the bombing of Iran just one day after it had nominated President Trump for a Nobel Peace Prize [6].

[2] US Urges China to Dissuade Iran From Closing Strait of Hormuz, https://www.usnews.com/news/world/articles/2025-06-22/us-urges-china-to-dissuade-iran-from-closing-strait-of-hormuz

**Topic 2.2: Regional Dynamics in the Middle East**

Multiple international news outlets are framing the strikes not as the start of a new, distinct conflict, but as the direct insertion of the United States military into the ongoing, long-term shadow war between Israel and Iran [1, 2]. This strategic shift is being widely interpreted as a major political victory for Israeli Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu. One report from The New York Times claims the U.S. military action "cements Netanyahu’s political comeback" [3]. The prevailing analysis in these headlines is that the U.S., by its actions, has now formally joined an existing and volatile regional war, with profound and lasting consequences for its role in the Middle East [4].

**Area 3: Economic and National Security Consequences**

**Topic 3.1: Domestic Security and Global Energy Markets**

The strikes have generated immediate and tangible consequences for U.S. national security and the global economy. Citing the military action, the Department of Homeland Security has issued a national terrorism advisory bulletin, warning of a "heightened threat environment" inside the United States [1, 2]. Concurrently, global oil prices have soared as the attack "ramps up risks to supplies," a situation that could be severely exacerbated if Iran acts on its threat to close the Strait of Hormuz shipping route [3, 4]. This market volatility has led to immediate concerns that the American economy now faces a "potential war shock" driven by a rapid and sustained surge in global energy prices [5].

**Area 4: Domestic Political and Legal Response**

**Topic 4.1: Congressional Authority and Partisan Fractures**

President Trump's order to strike Iran has ignited a fierce constitutional debate over executive authority and has exposed deep and public divisions, including within the Republican party. The administration is actively defending the legality of the operation, while a growing number of Democratic lawmakers have labeled the action an "illegal" war and are demanding a formal congressional vote on the use of force [1, 2]. Representative Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez has stated the action is an "impeachment-worthy" offense, and a list of members backing a War Powers Resolution against the President is now circulating [3, 4]. The reaction from the political right has been fractured. A "MAGA Civil War" has reportedly erupted online, with President Trump publicly calling for his supporters to "drop ‘pathetic loser’ Massie" after the Republican representative voiced opposition to the strikes [5, 6]. Another Republican congressman stated it was "'Ludicrous' to say the Iran strikes are not an act of war," while Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene posted that "Peace Is The Answer" [7, 8].

## 2. International Ramifications of the U.S. Strikes

### 2.1. Global Diplomatic Reactions and Iranian Response

The U.S. strikes have triggered sharp international condemnation and threats of dangerous escalation. In a particularly severe development, Russia has publicly claimed that other unnamed nations are now "ready to supply Iran with nukes" in the direct aftermath of the U.S. action [1]. In a bid to control the economic fallout, the U.S. has publicly urged China to leverage its influence to "dissuade Iran from closing Strait of Hormuz" [2]. This diplomatic outreach comes as Iran's parliament has reportedly backed measures to do just that, with Iranian Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi warning of "everlasting consequences" for the strikes [3, 4]. Meanwhile, reports from inside Iran describe a population that feels "'paralysed and constantly caught by surprise'" by the attack [5]. In another significant diplomatic reversal, Pakistan issued a statement condemning the bombing of Iran just one day after it had nominated President Trump for a Nobel Peace Prize [6].

### 2.2. Regional Dynamics in the Middle East

Multiple international news outlets are framing the strikes not as the start of a new, distinct conflict, but as the direct insertion of the United States military into the ongoing, long-term shadow war between Israel and Iran [1, 2]. This strategic shift is being widely interpreted as a major political victory for Israeli Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu. One report from The New York Times claims the U.S. military action "cements Netanyahu’s political comeback" [3]. The prevailing analysis in these headlines is that the U.S., by its actions, has now formally joined an existing and volatile regional war, with profound and lasting consequences for its role in the Middle East [4].

## 3. Economic and National Security Consequences

### 3.1. Domestic Security and Global Energy Markets

The strikes have generated immediate and tangible consequences for U.S. national security and the global economy. Citing the military action, the Department of Homeland Security has issued a national terrorism advisory bulletin, warning of a "heightened threat environment" inside the United States [1, 2]. Concurrently, global oil prices have soared as the attack "ramps up risks to supplies," a situation that could be severely exacerbated if Iran acts on its threat to close the Strait of Hormuz shipping route [3, 4]. This market volatility has led to immediate concerns that the American economy now faces a "potential war shock" driven by a rapid and sustained surge in global energy prices [5].

## 4. Domestic Political and Legal Response

### 4.1. Congressional Authority and Partisan Fractures

President Trump's order to strike Iran has ignited a fierce constitutional debate over executive authority and has exposed deep and public divisions, including within the Republican party. The administration is actively defending the legality of the operation, while a growing number of Democratic lawmakers have labeled the action an "illegal" war and are demanding a formal congressional vote on the use of force [1, 2]. Representative Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez has stated the action is an "impeachment-worthy" offense, and a list of members backing a War Powers Resolution against the President is now circulating [3, 4]. The reaction from the political right has been fractured. A "MAGA Civil War" has reportedly erupted online, with President Trump publicly calling for his supporters to "drop ‘pathetic loser’ Massie" after the Republican representative voiced opposition to the strikes [5, 6]. Another Republican congressman stated it was "'Ludicrous' to say the Iran strikes are not an act of war," while Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene posted that "Peace Is The Answer" [7, 8].
